 8779     private NodeEventDispatcher getInternalEventDispatcher() {
 8780         initializeInternalEventDispatcher();
 8781         return internalEventDispatcher;
 8782     }
 8783 
 8784     private void initializeInternalEventDispatcher() {
 8785         if (internalEventDispatcher == null) {
 8786             internalEventDispatcher = createInternalEventDispatcher();
 8787             eventDispatcher = new SimpleObjectProperty<EventDispatcher>(
 8788                                           Node.this,
 8789                                           "eventDispatcher",
 8790                                           internalEventDispatcher);
 8791         }
 8792     }
 8793 
 8794     private NodeEventDispatcher createInternalEventDispatcher() {
 8795         return new NodeEventDispatcher(this);
 8796     }
 8797 
 8798     /**
 8799      * Event dispatcher for invoking preprocessing of mouse events
 8800      */
 8801     private EventDispatcher preprocessMouseEventDispatcher;
 8802 
 8803     // PENDING_DOC_REVIEW
 8804     /**
 8805      * Construct an event dispatch chain for this node. The event dispatch chain
 8806      * contains all event dispatchers from the stage to this node.
 8807      *
 8808      * @param tail the initial chain to build from
 8809      * @return the resulting event dispatch chain for this node
 8810      */
 8811     @Override
 8812     public EventDispatchChain buildEventDispatchChain(
 8813             EventDispatchChain tail) {
 8814 
 8815         if (preprocessMouseEventDispatcher == null) {
 8816             preprocessMouseEventDispatcher = (event, tail1) -> {
 8817                 event = tail1.dispatchEvent(event);
 8818                 if (event instanceof MouseEvent) {
 8819                     preprocessMouseEvent((MouseEvent) event);
 8820                 }
 8821 
 8822                 return event;
 8823             };
 8824         }
 8825 
 8826         tail = tail.prepend(preprocessMouseEventDispatcher);
 8827 
 8828         // prepend all event dispatchers from this node to the root
 8829         Node curNode = this;
 8830         do {
 8831             if (curNode.eventDispatcher != null) {
 8832                 final EventDispatcher eventDispatcherValue =
 8833                         curNode.eventDispatcher.get();
 8834                 if (eventDispatcherValue != null) {
 8835                     tail = tail.prepend(eventDispatcherValue);
 8836                 }
 8837             }
 8838             final Node curParent = curNode.getParent();
 8839             curNode = curParent != null ? curParent : curNode.getSubScene();
 8840         } while (curNode != null);
 8841 
 8842         if (getScene() != null) {
 8843             // prepend scene's dispatch chain
 8844             tail = getScene().buildEventDispatchChain(tail);
 8845         }
 8846 
 8847         return tail;
 8848     }
 8849 
 8850     // PENDING_DOC_REVIEW
 8851     /**
 8852      * Fires the specified event. By default the event will travel through the
 8853      * hierarchy from the stage to this node. Any event filter encountered will
 8854      * be notified and can consume the event. If not consumed by the filters,
 8855      * the event handlers on this node are notified. If these don't consume the
 8856      * event either, the event will travel back the same path it arrived to
 8857      * this node. All event handlers encountered are called and can consume the
 8858      * event.
 8859      * <p>
 8860      * This method must be called on the FX user thread.
 8861      *
 8862      * @param event the event to fire
 8863      */
 8864     public final void fireEvent(Event event) {
 8865 
 8866         /* Log input events.  We do a coarse filter for at least the FINE
 8867          * level and then granularize from there.
 8868          */
 8869         if (event instanceof InputEvent) {
 8870             PlatformLogger logger = Logging.getInputLogger();
 8871             if (logger.isLoggable(Level.FINE)) {
 8872                 EventType eventType = event.getEventType();
 8873                 if (eventType == MouseEvent.MOUSE_ENTERED ||
 8874                     eventType == MouseEvent.MOUSE_EXITED) {
 8875                     logger.finer(event.toString());
 8876                 } else if (eventType == MouseEvent.MOUSE_MOVED ||
 8877                            eventType == MouseEvent.MOUSE_DRAGGED) {
 8878                     logger.finest(event.toString());
 8879                 } else {
 8880                     logger.fine(event.toString());
 8881                 }
 8882             }
 8883         }
 8884 
 8885         Event.fireEvent(this, event);
 8886     }

 8889      *                                                                         *
 8890      *                         Stylesheet Handling                             *
 8891      *                                                                         *
 8892      **************************************************************************/

 8895     /**
 8896      * {@inheritDoc}
 8897      * @return {@code getClass().getName()} without the package name
 8898      * @since JavaFX 8.0
 8899      */
 8900     @Override
 8901     public String getTypeSelector() {
 8902 
 8903         final Class<?> clazz = getClass();
 8904         final Package pkg = clazz.getPackage();
 8905 
 8906         // package could be null. not likely, but could be.
 8907         int plen = 0;
 8908         if (pkg != null) {
 8909             plen = pkg.getName().length();
 8910         }
 8911 
 8912         final int clen = clazz.getName().length();
 8913         final int pos = (0 < plen && plen < clen) ? plen + 1 : 0;
 8914 
 8915         return clazz.getName().substring(pos);
 8916     }

 8925         return getParent();
 8926     }

 9223     /**
 9224      * @return The CssMetaData associated with this class, which may include the
 9225      * CssMetaData of its superclasses.
 9226      * @since JavaFX 8.0
 9227      */
 9228     public static List<CssMetaData<? extends Styleable, ?>> getClassCssMetaData() {
 9229         //
 9230         // Super-lazy instantiation pattern from Bill Pugh. StyleableProperties
 9231         // is referenced no earlier (and therefore loaded no earlier by the
 9232         // class loader) than the moment that  getClassCssMetaData() is called.
 9233         // This avoids loading the CssMetaData instances until the point at
 9234         // which CSS needs the data.
 9235         //
 9236         return StyleableProperties.STYLEABLES;
 9237     }
 9238 
 9239     /**
 9240      * This method should delegate to {@link Node#getClassCssMetaData()} so that
 9241      * a Node's CssMetaData can be accessed without the need for reflection.
 9242      *
 9243      * @return The CssMetaData associated with this node, which may include the
 9244      * CssMetaData of its superclasses.
 9245      * @since JavaFX 8.0
 9246      */
 9247 
 9248     @Override
 9249     public List<CssMetaData<? extends Styleable, ?>> getCssMetaData() {
 9250         return getClassCssMetaData();
 9251     }

 9254      * @return  The Styles that match this CSS property for the given Node. The
 9255      * list is sorted by descending specificity.
 9256      */
 9257     // SB-dependency: RT-21096 has been filed to track this
 9258     static List<Style> getMatchingStyles(CssMetaData cssMetaData, Styleable styleable) {
 9259          return CssStyleHelper.getMatchingStyles(styleable, cssMetaData);
 9260     }
 9261 
 9262     final ObservableMap<StyleableProperty<?>, List<Style>> getStyleMap() {
 9263          ObservableMap<StyleableProperty<?>, List<Style>> map =
 9264                  (ObservableMap<StyleableProperty<?>, List<Style>>)getProperties().get("STYLEMAP");
 9265          Map<StyleableProperty<?>, List<Style>> ret = CssStyleHelper.getMatchingStyles(map, this);
 9266          if (ret != null) {
 9267              if (ret instanceof ObservableMap) return (ObservableMap)ret;
 9268              return FXCollections.observableMap(ret);
 9269          }
 9270          return FXCollections.<StyleableProperty<?>, List<Style>>emptyObservableMap();
 9271      }
 9272 
 9273      /*
 9274       * RT-17293
 9275       */
 9276      // SB-dependency: RT-21096 has been filed to track this
 9277      final void setStyleMap(ObservableMap<StyleableProperty<?>, List<Style>> styleMap) {
 9278          if (styleMap != null) getProperties().put("STYLEMAP", styleMap);
 9279          else getProperties().remove("STYLEMAP");
 9280      }

 9282     /*
 9283      * Find CSS styles that were used to style this Node in its current pseudo-class state. The map will contain the styles from this node and,
 9284      * if the node is a Parent, its children. The node corresponding to an entry in the Map can be obtained by casting a StyleableProperty key to a
 9285      * javafx.beans.property.Property and calling getBean(). The List contains only those styles used to style the property and will contain
 9286      * styles used to resolve lookup values.
 9287      *
 9288      * @param styleMap A Map to be populated with the styles. If null, a new Map will be allocated.
 9289      * @return The Map populated with matching styles.
 9290      */
 9291     // SB-dependency: RT-21096 has been filed to track this
 9292     Map<StyleableProperty<?>,List<Style>> findStyles(Map<StyleableProperty<?>,List<Style>> styleMap) {
 9293 
 9294         Map<StyleableProperty<?>, List<Style>> ret = CssStyleHelper.getMatchingStyles(styleMap, this);
 9295         return (ret != null) ? ret : Collections.<StyleableProperty<?>, List<Style>>emptyMap();
 9296     }
 9297 
 9298     /**
 9299      * Flags used to indicate in which way this node is dirty (or whether it
 9300      * is clean) and what must happen during the next CSS cycle on the
 9301      * scenegraph.
 9302      */
 9303     CssFlags cssFlag = CssFlags.CLEAN;
 9304 
 9305     /**
 9306      * Needed for testing.
 9307      */
 9308     final CssFlags getCSSFlags() { return cssFlag; }
 9309 
 9310     /**
 9311      * Called when a CSS pseudo-class change would cause styles to be reapplied.
 9312      */
 9313     private void requestCssStateTransition() {
 9314         // If there is no scene, then we cannot make it dirty, so we'll leave
 9315         // the flag alone
 9316         if (getScene() == null) return;
 9317         // Don't bother doing anything if the cssFlag is not CLEAN.
 9318         // If the flag indicates a DIRTY_BRANCH, the flag needs to be changed
 9319         // to UPDATE to ensure that NodeHelper.processCSS is called on the node.
 9320         if (cssFlag == CssFlags.CLEAN || cssFlag == CssFlags.DIRTY_BRANCH) {
 9321             cssFlag = CssFlags.UPDATE;
 9322             notifyParentsOfInvalidatedCSS();
 9323         }
 9324     }
 9325 
 9326     /**
 9327      * Used to specify that a pseudo-class of this Node has changed. If the
 9328      * pseudo-class is used in a CSS selector that matches this Node, CSS will
 9329      * be reapplied. Typically, this method is called from the {@code invalidated}
 9330      * method of a property that is used as a pseudo-class. For example:
 9331      * <pre><code>
 9332      *
 9333      *     private static final PseudoClass MY_PSEUDO_CLASS_STATE = PseudoClass.getPseudoClass("my-state");
 9334      *
 9335      *     BooleanProperty myPseudoClassState = new BooleanPropertyBase(false) {
 9336      *
 9337      *           {@literal @}Override public void invalidated() {
 9338      *                pseudoClassStateChanged(MY_PSEUDO_CLASS_STATE, get());
 9339      *           }
 9340      *
 9341      *           {@literal @}Override public Object getBean() {
 9342      *               return MyControl.this;
 9343      *           }
 9344      *
 9345      *           {@literal @}Override public String getName() {
 9346      *               return "myPseudoClassState";
 9347      *           }
 9348      *       };
 9349      * </code></pre>
 9350      * @param pseudoClass the pseudo-class that has changed state
 9351      * @param active whether or not the state is active
 9352      * @since JavaFX 8.0
 9353      */
 9354     public final void pseudoClassStateChanged(PseudoClass pseudoClass, boolean active) {
 9355 
 9356         final boolean modified = active
 9357                 ? pseudoClassStates.add(pseudoClass)
 9358                 : pseudoClassStates.remove(pseudoClass);
 9359 
 9360         if (modified && styleHelper != null) {
 9361             final boolean isTransition = styleHelper.pseudoClassStateChanged(pseudoClass);
 9362             if (isTransition) {
 9363                 requestCssStateTransition();
 9364             }
 9365         }
 9366    }
 9367 
 9368     // package so that StyleHelper can get at it
 9369     final ObservableSet<PseudoClass> pseudoClassStates = new PseudoClassState();
 9370     private final ObservableSet<PseudoClass> unmodifiablePseudoClassStates =
 9371             FXCollections.unmodifiableObservableSet(pseudoClassStates);
 9372     /**
 9373      * @return The active pseudo-class states of this Node, wrapped in an unmodifiable ObservableSet
 9374      * @since JavaFX 8.0
 9375      */
 9376     @Override
 9377     public final ObservableSet<PseudoClass> getPseudoClassStates() {
 9378         return unmodifiablePseudoClassStates;
 9379     }
 9380 
 9381     // Walks up the tree telling each parent that the pseudo class state of
 9382     // this node has changed.
 9383     final void notifyParentsOfInvalidatedCSS() {
 9384         SubScene subScene = getSubScene();
 9385         Parent root = (subScene != null) ?
 9386                 subScene.getRoot() : getScene().getRoot();
 9387 
 9388         if (!root.isDirty(DirtyBits.NODE_CSS)) {
 9389             // Ensure that Scene.root is marked as dirty. If the scene isn't
 9390             // dirty, nothing will get repainted. This bit is cleared from
 9391             // Scene in doCSSPass().
 9392             NodeHelper.markDirty(root, DirtyBits.NODE_CSS);
 9393             if (subScene != null) {
 9394                 // If the node is part of a subscene, then we must ensure that
 9395                 // the we not only mark subScene.root dirty, but continue and
 9396                 // call subScene.notifyParentsOfInvalidatedCSS() until
 9397                 // Scene.root gets marked dirty, via the recursive call:
 9398                 subScene.cssFlag = CssFlags.UPDATE;
 9399                 subScene.notifyParentsOfInvalidatedCSS();
 9400             }
 9401         }
 9402         Parent _parent = getParent();
 9403         while (_parent != null) {
 9404             if (_parent.cssFlag == CssFlags.CLEAN) {
 9405                 _parent.cssFlag = CssFlags.DIRTY_BRANCH;
 9406                 _parent = _parent.getParent();
 9407             } else {
 9408                 _parent = null;
 9409             }
 9410         }
 9411     }
 9412 
 9413     final void reapplyCSS() {
 9414 
 9415         if (getScene() == null) return;
 9416 
 9417         if (cssFlag == CssFlags.REAPPLY) return;
 9418 
 9419         if (cssFlag == CssFlags.DIRTY_BRANCH) {
 9420             // JDK-8193445 - don't reapply CSS from here
 9421             // Defer CSS application to this Node by marking cssFlag as REAPPLY
 9422             cssFlag = CssFlags.REAPPLY;
 9423             return;
 9424         }
 9425 
 9426         // RT-36838 - don't reapply CSS in the middle of an update
 9427         if (cssFlag == CssFlags.UPDATE) {
 9428             cssFlag = CssFlags.REAPPLY;
 9429             notifyParentsOfInvalidatedCSS();
 9430             return;
 9431         }
 9432 
 9433         reapplyCss();
 9434 
 9435         //
 9436         // One idiom employed by developers is to, during the layout pass,
 9437         // add or remove nodes from the scene. For example, a ScrollPane
 9438         // might add scroll bars to itself if it determines during layout
 9439         // that it needs them, or a ListView might add cells to itself if
 9440         // it determines that it needs to. In such situations we must
 9441         // apply the CSS immediately and not add it to the scene's queue
 9442         // for deferred action.
 9443         //
 9444         if (getParent() != null && getParent().isPerformingLayout()) {
 9445             NodeHelper.processCSS(this);
 9446         } else {
 9447             notifyParentsOfInvalidatedCSS();
 9448         }
 9449 
 9450     }
 9451 
 9452     //
 9453     // This method "reapplies" CSS to this node and all of its children. Reapplying CSS
 9454     // means that new style maps are calculated for the node. The process of reapplying
 9455     // CSS may reset the CSS properties of a node to their initial state, but the _new_
 9456     // styles are not applied as part of this process.
 9457     //
 9458     // There is no check of the CSS state of a child since reapply takes precedence
 9459     // over other CSS states.
 9460     //
 9461     private void reapplyCss() {
 9462 
 9463         // Hang on to current styleHelper so we can know whether
 9464         // createStyleHelper returned the same styleHelper
 9465         final CssStyleHelper oldStyleHelper = styleHelper;
 9466 
 9467         // CSS state is "REAPPLY"
 9468         cssFlag = CssFlags.REAPPLY;
 9469 
 9470         styleHelper = CssStyleHelper.createStyleHelper(this);
 9471 
 9472         // REAPPLY to my children, too.
 9473         if (this instanceof Parent) {
 9474 
 9475             // minor optimization to avoid calling createStyleHelper on children
 9476             // when we know there will not be any change in the style maps.
 9477             final boolean visitChildren =
 9478                     // If we don't have a styleHelper, then we should visit the children of this parent
 9479                     // since there might be styles that depend on being a child of this parent.
 9480                     // In other words, we have .a > .b { blah: blort; }, but no styles for ".a" itself.
 9481                     styleHelper == null ||
 9482                     // if the styleHelper changed, then we definitely need to visit the children
 9483                     // since the new styles may have an effect on the children's styles calculated values.
 9484                     (oldStyleHelper != styleHelper) ||
 9485                     // If our parent is null, then we're the root of a scene or sub-scene, most likely,
 9486                     // and we'll visit children because elsewhere the code depends on root.reapplyCSS()
 9487                     // to force css to be reapplied (whether it needs to be or not).
 9488                     (getParent() == null) ||
 9489                     // If our parent's cssFlag is other than clean, then the parent may have just had
 9490                     // CSS reapplied. If the parent just had CSS reapplied, then some of its styles
 9491                     // may affect my children's styles.
 9492                     (getParent().cssFlag != CssFlags.CLEAN);
 9493 
 9494             if (visitChildren) {
 9495 
 9496                 List<Node> children = ((Parent) this).getChildren();
 9497                 for (int n = 0, nMax = children.size(); n < nMax; n++) {
 9498                     Node child = children.get(n);
 9499                     child.reapplyCss();
 9500                 }
 9501             }
 9502 
 9503         } else if (this instanceof SubScene) {
 9504 
 9505             // SubScene root is a Parent, but reapplyCss is a private method in Node
 9506             final Node subSceneRoot = ((SubScene)this).getRoot();
 9507             if (subSceneRoot != null) {
 9508                 subSceneRoot.reapplyCss();
 9509             }
 9510 
 9511         } else if (styleHelper == null) {
 9512             //
 9513             // If this is not a Parent and there is no styleHelper, then the CSS state is "CLEAN"
 9514             // since there are no styles to apply or children to update.
 9515             //
 9516             cssFlag = CssFlags.CLEAN;
 9517             return;
 9518         }
 9519 
 9520         cssFlag = CssFlags.UPDATE;
 9521 
 9522     }
 9523 
 9524     void processCSS() {
 9525         switch (cssFlag) {
 9526             case CLEAN:
 9527                 break;
 9528             case DIRTY_BRANCH:
 9529             {
 9530                 Parent me = (Parent)this;
 9531                 // clear the flag first in case the flag is set to something
 9532                 // other than clean by downstream processing.
 9533                 me.cssFlag = CssFlags.CLEAN;
 9534                 List<Node> children = me.getChildren();
 9535                 for (int i=0, max=children.size(); i<max; i++) {
 9536                     children.get(i).processCSS();
 9537                 }
 9538                 break;
 9539             }
 9540             case REAPPLY:
 9541             case UPDATE:
 9542             default:
 9543                 NodeHelper.processCSS(this);
 9544         }
 9545     }
 9546 
 9547     /**
 9548      * If required, apply styles to this Node and its children, if any. This method does not normally need to
 9549      * be invoked directly but may be used in conjunction with {@link Parent#layout()} to size a Node before the
 9550      * next pulse, or if the {@link #getScene() Scene} is not in a {@link javafx.stage.Stage}.
 9551      * <p>Provided that the Node&#39;s {@link #getScene() Scene} is not null, CSS is applied to this Node regardless
 9552      * of whether this Node&#39;s CSS state is clean. CSS styles are applied from the top-most parent
 9553      * of this Node whose CSS state is other than clean, which may affect the styling of other nodes.
 9554      * This method is a no-op if the Node is not in a Scene. The Scene does not have to be in a Stage.</p>
 9555      * <p>This method does not invoke the {@link Parent#layout()} method. Typically, the caller will use the
 9556      * following sequence of operations.</p>
 9557      * <pre>{@code
 9558      *     parentNode.applyCss();
 9559      *     parentNode.layout();
 9560      * }</pre>
 9561      * <p>As a more complete example, the following code uses {@code applyCss()} and {@code layout()} to find
 9562      * the width and height of the Button before the Stage has been shown. If either the call to {@code applyCss()}
 9563      * or the call to {@code layout()} is commented out, the calls to {@code getWidth()} and {@code getHeight()}
 9564      * will return zero (until some time after the Stage is shown). </p>
 9565      * <pre><code>
 9566      * {@literal @}Override
 9567      * public void start(Stage stage) throws Exception {
 9568      *
 9569      *    Group root = new Group();
 9570      *    Scene scene = new Scene(root);
 9571      *
 9572      *    Button button = new Button("Hello World");
 9573      *    root.getChildren().add(button);
 9574      *
 9575      *    root.applyCss();
 9576      *    root.layout();
 9577      *
 9578      *    double width = button.getWidth();
 9579      *    double height = button.getHeight();
 9580      *
 9581      *    System.out.println(width + ", " + height);
 9582      *
 9583      *    stage.setScene(scene);
 9584      *    stage.show();
 9585      * }
 9586      * </code></pre>
 9587      * @since JavaFX 8.0
 9588      */
 9589     public final void applyCss() {
 9590 
 9591         if (getScene() == null) {
 9592             return;
 9593         }
 9594 
 9595         // update, unless reapply
 9596         if (cssFlag != CssFlags.REAPPLY) cssFlag = CssFlags.UPDATE;
 9597 
 9598         //
 9599         // RT-28394 - need to see if any ancestor has a flag UPDATE
 9600         // If so, process css from the top-most CssFlags.UPDATE node
 9601         // since my ancestor's styles may affect mine.
 9602         //
 9603         // If the scene-graph root isn't NODE_CSS dirty, then all my
 9604         // ancestor flags should be CLEAN and I can skip this lookup.
 9605         //
 9606         Node topMost = this;
 9607 
 9608         final boolean dirtyRoot = getScene().getRoot().isDirty(com.sun.javafx.scene.DirtyBits.NODE_CSS);
 9609         if (dirtyRoot) {
 9610 
 9611             Node _parent = getParent();
 9612             while (_parent != null) {
 9613                 if (_parent.cssFlag == CssFlags.UPDATE || _parent.cssFlag == CssFlags.REAPPLY) {
 9614                     topMost = _parent;
 9615                 }
 9616                 _parent = _parent.getParent();
 9617             }
 9618 
 9619             // Note: this code used to mark the parent nodes with DIRTY_BRANCH,
 9620             // but that isn't necessary since UPDATE will apply css to all of
 9621             // a Parent's children.
 9622 
 9623             // If we're at the root of the scene-graph, make sure the NODE_CSS
 9624             // dirty bit is cleared (see Scene#doCSSPass())
 9625             if (topMost == getScene().getRoot()) {
 9626                 getScene().getRoot().clearDirty(DirtyBits.NODE_CSS);
 9627             }
 9628         }
 9629 
 9630         topMost.processCSS();
 9631 
 9632     }
 9633 
 9634     /*
 9635      * If invoked, will update styles from here on down. This method should not be called directly. If
 9636      * overridden, the overriding method must at some point call {@code super.processCSSImpl} to ensure that
 9637      * this Node's CSS state is properly updated.
 9638      *
 9639      * Note that the difference between this method and {@link #applyCss()} is that this method
 9640      * updates styles for this node on down; whereas, {@code applyCss()} looks for the top-most ancestor that needs
 9641      * CSS update and apply styles from that node on down.
 9642      *
 9643      * Note: This method MUST only be called via its accessor method.
 9644      */
 9645     private void doProcessCSS() {
 9646 
 9647         // Nothing to do...
 9648         if (cssFlag == CssFlags.CLEAN) return;
 9649 
 9650         // if REAPPLY was deferred, process it now...
 9651         if (cssFlag == CssFlags.REAPPLY) {
 9652             reapplyCss();
 9653         }
 9654 
 9655         // Clear the flag first in case the flag is set to something
 9656         // other than clean by downstream processing.
 9657         cssFlag = CssFlags.CLEAN;
 9658 
 9659         // Transition to the new state and apply styles
 9660         if (styleHelper != null && getScene() != null) {
 9661             styleHelper.transitionToState(this);
 9662         }
 9663     }
 9664 
 9665 
 9666     /**
 9667      * A StyleHelper for this node.
 9668      * A StyleHelper contains all the css styles for this node
 9669      * and knows how to apply them when our state changes.
 9670      */
 9671     CssStyleHelper styleHelper;
 9672 
 9673     private static final PseudoClass HOVER_PSEUDOCLASS_STATE = PseudoClass.getPseudoClass("hover");
 9674     private static final PseudoClass PRESSED_PSEUDOCLASS_STATE = PseudoClass.getPseudoClass("pressed");
 9675     private static final PseudoClass DISABLED_PSEUDOCLASS_STATE = PseudoClass.getPseudoClass("disabled");
 9676     private static final PseudoClass FOCUSED_PSEUDOCLASS_STATE = PseudoClass.getPseudoClass("focused");
 9677     private static final PseudoClass SHOW_MNEMONICS_PSEUDOCLASS_STATE = PseudoClass.getPseudoClass("show-mnemonics");

 9679     private static abstract class LazyTransformProperty
 9680             extends ReadOnlyObjectProperty<Transform> {
 9681 
 9682         protected static final int VALID = 0;
 9683         protected static final int INVALID = 1;
 9684         protected static final int VALIDITY_UNKNOWN = 2;
 9685         protected int valid = INVALID;
 9686 
 9687         private ExpressionHelper<Transform> helper;
 9688 
 9689         private Transform transform;
 9690         private boolean canReuse = false;
 9691 
 9692         @Override
 9693         public void addListener(InvalidationListener listener) {
 9694             helper = ExpressionHelper.addListener(helper, this, listener);
 9695         }
 9696 
 9697         @Override
 9698         public void removeListener(InvalidationListener listener) {
 9699             helper = ExpressionHelper.removeListener(helper, listener);
 9700         }
 9701 
 9702         @Override
 9703         public void addListener(ChangeListener<? super Transform> listener) {
 9704             helper = ExpressionHelper.addListener(helper, this, listener);
 9705         }
 9706 
 9707         @Override
 9708         public void removeListener(ChangeListener<? super Transform> listener) {
 9709             helper = ExpressionHelper.removeListener(helper, listener);
 9710         }
 9711 
 9712         protected Transform getInternalValue() {
 9713             if (valid == INVALID ||
 9714                     (valid == VALIDITY_UNKNOWN && computeValidity() == INVALID)) {
 9715                 transform = computeTransform(canReuse ? transform : null);
 9716                 canReuse = true;
 9717                 valid = validityKnown() ? VALID : VALIDITY_UNKNOWN;
 9718             }
 9719 
 9720             return transform;
 9721         }
 9722 
 9723         @Override
 9724         public Transform get() {
 9725             transform = getInternalValue();
 9726             canReuse = false;
 9727             return transform;
 9728         }
 9729 
 9730         public void validityUnknown() {
 9731             if (valid == VALID) {
 9732                 valid = VALIDITY_UNKNOWN;
 9733             }
 9734         }
 9735 
 9736         public void invalidate() {
 9737             if (valid != INVALID) {
 9738                 valid = INVALID;
 9739                 ExpressionHelper.fireValueChangedEvent(helper);
 9740             }
 9741         }
 9742 
 9743         protected abstract boolean validityKnown();
 9744         protected abstract int computeValidity();
 9745         protected abstract Transform computeTransform(Transform reuse);
 9746     }
 9747 
 9748     private static abstract class LazyBoundsProperty
 9749             extends ReadOnlyObjectProperty<Bounds> {
 9750         private ExpressionHelper<Bounds> helper;
 9751         private boolean valid;
 9752 
 9753         private Bounds bounds;
 9754 
 9755         @Override
 9756         public void addListener(InvalidationListener listener) {
 9757             helper = ExpressionHelper.addListener(helper, this, listener);
 9758         }
 9759 
 9760         @Override
 9761         public void removeListener(InvalidationListener listener) {
 9762             helper = ExpressionHelper.removeListener(helper, listener);
 9763         }
 9764 
 9765         @Override
 9766         public void addListener(ChangeListener<? super Bounds> listener) {
 9767             helper = ExpressionHelper.addListener(helper, this, listener);
 9768         }
 9769 
 9770         @Override
 9771         public void removeListener(ChangeListener<? super Bounds> listener) {
 9772             helper = ExpressionHelper.removeListener(helper, listener);
 9773         }
 9774 
 9775         @Override
 9776         public Bounds get() {
 9777             if (!valid) {
 9778                 bounds = computeBounds();
 9779                 valid = true;
 9780             }
 9781 
 9782             return bounds;
 9783         }
 9784 
 9785         public void invalidate() {
 9786             if (valid) {
 9787                 valid = false;
 9788                 ExpressionHelper.fireValueChangedEvent(helper);
 9789             }
 9790         }
 9791 
 9792         protected abstract Bounds computeBounds();
 9793     }

 9797     /**
 9798      * The accessible role for this {@code Node}.
 9799      * <p>
 9800      * The screen reader uses the role of a node to determine the
 9801      * attributes and actions that are supported.
 9802      *
 9803      * @defaultValue {@link AccessibleRole#NODE}
 9804      * @see AccessibleRole
 9805      *
 9806      * @since JavaFX 8u40
 9807      */
 9808     private ObjectProperty<AccessibleRole> accessibleRole;
 9809 
 9810     public final void setAccessibleRole(AccessibleRole value) {
 9811         if (value == null) value = AccessibleRole.NODE;
 9812         accessibleRoleProperty().set(value);
 9813     }
 9814 
 9815     public final AccessibleRole getAccessibleRole() {
 9816         if (accessibleRole == null) return AccessibleRole.NODE;
 9817         return accessibleRoleProperty().get();
 9818     }

 9820     public final ObjectProperty<AccessibleRole> accessibleRoleProperty() {
 9821         if (accessibleRole == null) {
 9822             accessibleRole = new SimpleObjectProperty<AccessibleRole>(this, "accessibleRole", AccessibleRole.NODE);
 9823         }
 9824         return accessibleRole;
 9825     }
 9826 
 9827     public final void setAccessibleRoleDescription(String value) {
 9828         accessibleRoleDescriptionProperty().set(value);
 9829     }

 9832         if (accessibilityProperties == null) return null;
 9833         if (accessibilityProperties.accessibleRoleDescription == null) return null;
 9834         return accessibleRoleDescriptionProperty().get();
 9835     }

 9837     /**
 9838      * The role description of this {@code Node}.
 9839      * <p>
 9840      * Normally, when a role is provided for a node, the screen reader
 9841      * speaks the role as well as the contents of the node.  When this
 9842      * value is set, it is possible to override the default.  This is
 9843      * useful because the set of roles is predefined.  For example,
 9844      * it is possible to set the role of a node to be a button, but
 9845      * have the role description be arbitrary text.
 9846      *
 9847      * @return the role description of this {@code Node}.
 9848      * @defaultValue null
 9849      *
 9850      * @since JavaFX 8u40
 9851      */

 9853         return getAccessibilityProperties().getAccessibleRoleDescription();
 9854     }

 9858     }

 9861         if (accessibilityProperties == null) return null;
 9862         if (accessibilityProperties.accessibleText == null) return null;
 9863         return accessibleTextProperty().get();
 9864     }

 9866     /**
 9867      * The accessible text for this {@code Node}.
 9868      * <p>
 9869      * This property is used to set the text that the screen
 9870      * reader will speak.  If a node normally speaks text,
 9871      * that text is overriden.  For example, a button
 9872      * usually speaks using the text in the control but will
 9873      * no longer do this when this value is set.
 9874      *

 9876      * @defaultValue null

 9886     }

 9890         if (accessibilityProperties.accessibleHelp == null) return null;

 9918     private class AccessibilityProperties {
 9919         ObjectProperty<String> accessibleRoleDescription;
 9920         ObjectProperty<String> getAccessibleRoleDescription() {
 9921             if (accessibleRoleDescription == null) {
 9922                 accessibleRoleDescription = new SimpleObjectProperty<String>(Node.this, "accessibleRoleDescription", null);
 9923             }
 9924             return accessibleRoleDescription;
 9925         }
 9926         ObjectProperty<String> accessibleText;
 9927         ObjectProperty<String> getAccessibleText() {
 9928             if (accessibleText == null) {
 9929                 accessibleText = new SimpleObjectProperty<String>(Node.this, "accessibleText", null);
 9930             }
 9931             return accessibleText;
 9932         }
 9933         ObjectProperty<String> accessibleHelp;
 9934         ObjectProperty<String> getAccessibleHelp() {
 9935             if (accessibleHelp == null) {
 9936                 accessibleHelp = new SimpleObjectProperty<String>(Node.this, "accessibleHelp", null);
 9937             }
 9938             return accessibleHelp;
 9939         }

 9941 
 9942     /**
 9943      * This method is called by the assistive technology to request
 9944      * the value for an attribute.
 9945      * <p>
 9946      * This method is commonly overridden by subclasses to implement
 9947      * attributes that are required for a specific role.<br>
 9948      * If a particular attribute is not handled, the superclass implementation
 9949      * must be called.
 9950      * </p>
 9951      *
 9952      * @param attribute the requested attribute
 9953      * @param parameters optional list of parameters
 9954      * @return the value for the requested attribute
 9955      *
 9956      * @see AccessibleAttribute
 9957      *
 9958      * @since JavaFX 8u40
 9959      */
 9960     public Object queryAccessibleAttribute(AccessibleAttribute attribute, Object... parameters) {
 9961         switch (attribute) {
 9962             case ROLE: return getAccessibleRole();
 9963             case ROLE_DESCRIPTION: return getAccessibleRoleDescription();
 9964             case TEXT: return getAccessibleText();
 9965             case HELP: return getAccessibleHelp();
 9966             case PARENT: return getParent();
 9967             case SCENE: return getScene();
 9968             case BOUNDS: return localToScreen(getBoundsInLocal());
 9969             case DISABLED: return isDisabled();
 9970             case FOCUSED: return isFocused();
 9971             case VISIBLE: return isVisible();
 9972             case LABELED_BY: return labeledBy;
 9973             default: return null;
 9974         }
 9975     }
 9976 
 9977     /**
 9978      * This method is called by the assistive technology to request the action
 9979      * indicated by the argument should be executed.
 9980      * <p>
 9981      * This method is commonly overridden by subclasses to implement
 9982      * action that are required for a specific role.<br>
 9983      * If a particular action is not handled, the superclass implementation
 9984      * must be called.
 9985      * </p>
 9986      *
 9987      * @param action the action to execute
 9988      * @param parameters optional list of parameters
 9989      *
 9990      * @see AccessibleAction
 9991      *
 9992      * @since JavaFX 8u40
 9993      */
 9994     public void executeAccessibleAction(AccessibleAction action, Object... parameters) {
 9995         switch (action) {
 9996             case REQUEST_FOCUS:
 9997                 if (isFocusTraversable()) {
 9998                     requestFocus();
 9999                 }
10000                 break;
10001             case SHOW_MENU: {
10002                 Bounds b = getBoundsInLocal();
10003                 Point2D pt = localToScreen(b.getMaxX(), b.getMaxY());
10004                 ContextMenuEvent event =
10005                     new ContextMenuEvent(ContextMenuEvent.CONTEXT_MENU_REQUESTED,
10006                     b.getMaxX(), b.getMaxY(), pt.getX(), pt.getY(),
10007                     false, new PickResult(this, b.getMaxX(), b.getMaxY()));
10008                 Event.fireEvent(this, event);
10009                 break;
10010             }
10011             default:
10012         }
10013     }
10014 
10015     /**
10016      * This method is called by the application to notify the assistive
10017      * technology that the value for an attribute has changed.
10018      *
10019      * @param attributes the attribute whose value has changed
10020      *
10021      * @see AccessibleAttribute
10022      *
10023      * @since JavaFX 8u40
10024      */
10025     public final void notifyAccessibleAttributeChanged(AccessibleAttribute attributes) {
10026         if (accessible == null) {
10027             Scene scene = getScene();
10028             if (scene != null) {
10029                 accessible = scene.removeAccessible(this);
10030             }
10031         }
10032         if (accessible != null) {
10033             accessible.sendNotification(attributes);
10034         }
10035     }
10036 
10037     Accessible accessible;
10038     Accessible getAccessible() {
10039         if (accessible == null) {
10040             Scene scene = getScene();
10041             /* It is possible the node was reparented and getAccessible()
10042              * is called before the pulse. Try to recycle the accessible
10043              * before creating a new one.
10044              * Note: this code relies that an accessible can never be on
10045              * more than one Scene#accMap. Thus, the only way
10046              * scene#removeAccessible() returns non-null is if the node
10047              * old scene and new scene are the same object.
10048              */
10049             if (scene != null) {
10050                 accessible = scene.removeAccessible(this);
10051             }
10052         }
10053         if (accessible == null) {
10054             accessible = Application.GetApplication().createAccessible();
10055             accessible.setEventHandler(new Accessible.EventHandler() {
10056                 @SuppressWarnings("deprecation")
10057                 @Override public AccessControlContext getAccessControlContext() {
10058                     Scene scene = getScene();
10059                     if (scene == null) {
10060                         /* This can happen during the release process of an accessible object. */
10061                         throw new RuntimeException("Accessbility requested for node not on a scene");
10062                     }
10063                     if (scene.getPeer() != null) {
10064                         return scene.getPeer().getAccessControlContext();
10065                     } else {
10066                         /* In some rare cases the accessible for a Node is needed
10067                          * before its scene is made visible. For example, the screen reader
10068                          * might ask a Menu for its ContextMenu before the ContextMenu
10069                          * is made visible. That is a problem because the Window for the
10070                          * ContextMenu is only created immediately before the first time
10071                          * it is shown.
10072                          */
10073                         return scene.acc;
10074                     }
10075                 }
10076                 @Override public Object getAttribute(AccessibleAttribute attribute, Object... parameters) {
10077                     return queryAccessibleAttribute(attribute, parameters);
10078                 }
10079                 @Override public void executeAction(AccessibleAction action, Object... parameters) {
10080                     executeAccessibleAction(action, parameters);
10081                 }
10082                 @Override public String toString() {
10083                     String klassName = Node.this.getClass().getName();
10084                     return klassName.substring(klassName.lastIndexOf('.')+1);
10085                 }
10086             });
10087         }
10088         return accessible;
10089     }
10090 
10091     void releaseAccessible() {
10092         Accessible acc = this.accessible;
10093         if (acc != null) {
10094             accessible = null;
10095             acc.dispose();
10096         }
10097     }
10098
